            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        
        
        
        
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Garcia is a pretty good little baseball player that can do a lot of things to help a Major League Baseball team win games, but he may not be a huge contributor in fantasy ball. Originally signed by the Rangers, the versatile player was traded to the White Sox in 2013 but he's not likely to receive regular playing time and will be in a stiff battle to simply receive an opening day assignment in The Show. Chicago has a lot of middle infield depth but Garcia does have a few things going for him. Firstly, he's extremely valuable and has experience playing second base, third base, shortstop and can handle all three outfield positions. Secondly, he has value on the bases with his above-average speed. At the plate, though, the switch-hitter can be overpowered and his aggressive nature works against him, as witnessed in 2013 when he was rushed to the majors and struggled with inconsistent playing time. Garcia will likely open 2014 in Triple-A but he could be one of the first players recalled in the event of an injury. (Marc Hulet)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Garcia can be a useful piece in deep AL-only leagues due to his versatility and speed, but don't expect him to have much value in mixed leagues, even if he lucks into unexpected playing time.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Garcia isn’t much at the plate, but can play multiple infield positions. While the White Sox have a giant hole at second to open the season, Garcia isn’t considered a candidate to compete for a starting role. He’ll more than likely open the year as a defensive replacement. (<a href="https://twitter.com/Chris_Cwik">Chris Cwik</a>)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Leury Garcia spent 2013-14 as a speedy glove-first utility player, playing an impressive seven positions (including designated hitter and pitcher) and swiping 18 bags, but batting just .179/.215/.215 with one home run in 119 games between the two seasons. Things did not go a lot different for him last year, as he spent most of the year at Triple-A and made it into just 18 contests for the White Sox -- 11 of which came in September and October. The Dominican native hit .214/.267/.214 and managed to notch just one stolen base, providing almost all of his value as a flexible -- but not particularly adept -- fielder. Indeed, his '15 highlight may have been his pitching appearance on Sept. 15 in which he threw a scoreless inning and notched a strikeout vs. Oakland in a 17-6 loss. Garcia holds a .267/.315/.354 line with 188 stolen bases in 573 career minor league games, and he is expected to begin next year at Triple-A once again as a backup bench option for the White Sox. With that in mind, his fantasy value is limited to very cheap speed in only the deepest of formats. (Dylan Higgins)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Garcia's career so far has been that of a backup utility player with the ability to swipe some bases and play all over the field (or even pitch) in a pinch. That did not change last season, and he is unlikely to suddenly break out and become a viable fantasy player any time soon.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>It was a positive development for Garcia to play more center field last year, but even with the utter lack of depth out there for the White Sox, it just doesn't seem likely that the 25-year-old Dominican will get any sort of extended look. He's played every position other than catcher and first base — including pitching and striking out Jason Pridie — but the fact is through 155 MLB games, he's hit just .188/.225/.237.  He should see more playing time than ever before on a rebuilding White Sox team — he's only twice had more than 100 major league plate appearances in a season — but there just isn't much to like here offensively. He could be a really, really cheap source of steals (206 in eight minor league seasons with a high of 51), but he would kill rates elsewhere to the point of not being valuable whatsoever. (@Brandon_Warne)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>There's speed and defensive versatility here, but nothing else. Outside of obscenely deep leagues, look elsewhere.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
